Slide 0: Understanding Area
  Text: Let's learn how to measure the flat space covered by a shape. We call this space the area of the shape. To measure it, we cover the surface completely with smaller, identical units. In math, we express this as: Area = covered surface space. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Can you look at your desk and imagine covering it with square papers?
  Example: Example 1: Review standard details: Area = covered surface space.

Slide 1: The Concept of Square Tiles
  Text: A square tile is a shape with four equal sides. It is the perfect unit for measuring area because squares fit together side-by-side without leaving gaps. In math, we express this as: 1 tile = 1 unit of area. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. How does using the same size of square tiles help us get an accurate measurement?
  Example: Example 2: Review standard details: 1 tile = 1 unit of area.

Slide 2: Covering Surfaces Perfectly
  Text: When we cover a shape to find its area, we must make sure there are no gaps or overlaps. Every square tile must touch the edge of the next tile. In math, we express this as: Total Area = Sum of all tiles. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. What would happen to our area count if some tiles overlapped each other?
  Example: Example 3: Review standard details: Total Area = Sum of all tiles.

Slide 3: Rows and Columns in a Grid
  Text: To organize our tiles, we arrange them in neat rows that go across and columns that go down. This arrangement forms a grid pattern on the surface. In math, we express this as: Grid = Rows x Columns. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Multiplying rows by columns gives the exact number of squares without counting them individually. Can you count the number of rows and columns on a tiled floor?
  Example: Example 4: Review standard details: Grid = Rows x Columns.

Slide 4: Counting Tiles by Rows
  [Current Image: images/math_w1_img1.png]
  Text: We can find the total area of a grid by adding the tiles in each row. If there are 4 rows with 4 tiles each, we add 4 four times. In math, we express this as: Total = 4 + 4 + 4 + 4 = 16. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Why is adding by rows faster than counting each tile one by one?
  Example: Example 5: Review standard details: Total = 4 + 4 + 4 + 4 = 16.

Slide 5: Counting Tiles by Columns
  Text: Just like adding by rows, we can also count tiles by columns. If we have 4 columns of 5 tiles, we add 5 four times to get the area. In math, we express this as: Total = 5 + 5 + 5 + 5 = 20. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Do we get the same total area if we count by columns instead of rows?
  Example: Example 6: Review standard details: Total = 5 + 5 + 5 + 5 = 20.

Slide 6: Area of a Grid Rectangle
  Text: Let's calculate the area of a rectangle made of tiles. We multiply the number of horizontal rows by the number of vertical columns to find the total units. In math, we express this as: Area = 3 rows x 4 columns = 12 tiles. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. If a grid has 3 rows and 4 columns, how many tiles are there?

Slide 7: Area of a Grid Square
  Text: A square grid has the same number of rows and columns. To find its area, we multiply this number by itself because all its sides are equal length. In math, we express this as: Area = 4 rows x 4 columns = 16 tiles. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. If a square grid has 4 rows, what is its total area in tiles?

Slide 8: Estimating Area of Large Spaces
  Text: Sometimes we do not have enough tiles to cover a large floor. We can place a few tiles along the sides and estimate the total by imagining the grid. In math, we express this as: Estimate = Rows x Columns. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. Slide 9: The Multiplicative Area Model
  Text: Multiplication is a powerful math tool that helps us find area instantly. Instead of counting 50 tiles individually, we multiply the rows by the columns to get the answer. In math, we express this as: Area = Rows x Columns. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. Slide 10: Introducing the Area Formula
  Text: We can write our grid rule as a standard mathematical formula: Area equals Length multiplied by Width. This formula works for all rectangles and squares. In math, we express this as: Area = Length x Width. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Multiplying rows by columns gives the exact number of squares without counting them individually. What do the letters L and W stand for in our area formula?
  Example: Example 11: Review standard details: Area = Length x Width.

Slide 11: Length and Width Explained
  [Current Image: images/math_w1_img2.png]
  Text: Length is the measurement of the longer side of a rectangle, and Width is the measurement of the shorter side. We measure both sides using the same units. In math, we express this as: Length = long side, Width = short side. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles.   Example: Example 12: Review standard details: Length = long side, Width = short side.

Slide 12: Calculating Rectangle Area
  Text: Let's use our new formula to find the area of a rectangle. If the length is 6 units and the width is 4 units, we multiply 6 by 4. In math, we express this as: Area = 6 units x 4 units = 24 square units. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Slide 13: The Square Area Formula
  Text: Since a square has equal sides, its length and width are the same. We write its formula as Area equals Side multiplied by Side, or Side squared. In math, we express this as: Area = Side x Side. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Multiplying rows by columns gives the exact number of squares without counting them individually. How is the square area formula different from the rectangle area formula?
  Example: Example 14: Review standard details: Area = Side x Side.

Slide 14: Calculating Square Area
  Text: Let's apply the square area formula. If a square has a side length of 5 units, we multiply 5 by 5 to find that the area is 25. In math, we express this as: Area = 5 units x 5 units = 25 square units. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Slide 22: Common Error: Overlapping Tiles
  Text: A common mistake when measuring area is letting the tiles overlap. This makes our count too small because some space is covered twice by the same tiles. In math, we express this as: Overlap = Incorrect area measurement. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid.   Example: Example 23: Review standard details: Overlap = Incorrect area measurement.

Slide 23: Common Error: Leaving Gaps
  Text: Another mistake is leaving gaps between tiles. Gaps make our area measurement inaccurate because we are not counting the empty space between the tiles. In math, we express this as: Gaps = Empty spaces in measurement. Let's learn and master this key mathematical concept. A square tile has equal sides, which makes it the standard base for measuring flat spaces. We must make sure that every tile lies flat and touches the edges of the neighboring tiles. Counting each unit one by one is simple, but multiplication makes the process much faster. The total area is directly related to the length and width of the covering grid. Multiplying rows by columns gives the exact number of squares without counting them individually. Why must tiles touch edge-to-edge to give a true area measurement?
  Example: Example 24: Review standard details: Gaps = Empty spaces in measurement.

Slide 24: Review of Area Concepts
  Text: Let's summarize what we learned. Area measures covered flat space. We cover shapes with square tiles, count them, or use the multiplication formula: Area equals Length times Width. Subject: SCIENCE
----------------------------------------
Slide 0: Welcome to the Science Adventure!
  Text: Hello, Young Scientist! Welcome to Science Week 1! This week we are starting an exciting journey of discovery. We will look closely at the world around us. Science helps us explain everything we observe every day. We will use our eyes, ears, and hands to study nature. We will learn how weather, plants, and water connect to science. Let's get ready to explore and learn together. Are you ready to observe like a real scientist? For instance, consider the example of Weekly Goal: Understand how science explains daily observations in nature. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Weekly Goal: Understand how science explains daily observations in nature.

Slide 1: Senses and Observation
  Text: Our sense organs are our windows to the world. We use our five senses to collect facts about nature. Our eyes see colors, shapes, and movements of objects. Our ears hear sounds like wind rustling leaves. Our nose smells flowers, and our tongue tastes food. Our skin feels heat, cold, and rough textures. An observation is a fact we gather using our senses. Let's practice observing our classroom objects today! For instance, consider the example of Observation: Using your eyes to see that a leaf is green and oval. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Observation: Using your eyes to see that a leaf is green and oval.

Slide 2: Weather in Daily Life
  Text: Weather is a natural event that we observe daily. Science helps us explain why the weather changes. The Sun gives us light and heat to keep us warm. Clouds form when water vapor rises and cools in the sky. Rain falls when clouds become too heavy with water. Wind is moving air that we can feel on our skin. Weather affects what we wear and what activities we do. What is the weather like outside your window right now? For instance, consider the example of Weather Fact: Rain falls from clouds when water droplets grow too heavy. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Weather Fact: Rain falls from clouds when water droplets grow too heavy.

Slide 3: Plants and Science
  Text: Plants are living things that grow all around us. They need sunlight, water, soil, and air to survive. A seed sprouts roots downwards to absorb water from soil. It grows a green stem upwards to capture sunlight. Plants use sunlight to make their own food in leaves. This active process is called photosynthesis in science. We observe plants bending towards window light to grow. Plants give us oxygen to breathe and food to eat! For instance, consider the example of Plant Growth: A seed needs water and sun to break its shell and grow roots. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Plant Growth: A seed needs water and sun to break its shell and grow roots.

Slide 4: Animals and Movement
  [Current Image: images/science_w1_img1.png]
  Text: Animals are living things that move in different ways. They move to find food, water, and safe shelters. Fish swim in water using their fins and tails. Birds fly through the air using wings and feathers. Frogs hop on land using their strong back legs. Crabs crawl sideways on the wet sand of beaches. Their body shapes help them survive in their habitats. Observe how a dog moves when it chases a toy! For instance, consider the example of Animal Fact: Fish have gills to breathe oxygen underwater while swimming. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Animal Fact: Fish have gills to breathe oxygen underwater while swimming.

Slide 5: Water Around Us
  Text: Water is a precious liquid found throughout nature. It exists in rivers, lakes, oceans, and rain clouds. We use water for drinking, washing, and growing crops. Water changes its form when heated or cooled down. Wet clothes dry because heat turns water into vapor. This process of turning liquid to gas is evaporation. Water always flows downwards from high to low ground. Let's observe water flowing down a sloped surface! For instance, consider the example of Water Flow: Gravity pulls flowing water downwards along riverbeds. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Water Flow: Gravity pulls flowing water downwards along riverbeds.

Slide 6: Light and Shadows
  Text: Light travels in straight lines from light sources. The Sun, lamps, and flashlights are light sources. When an object blocks light, a shadow forms behind it. A shadow is a dark shape on a surface behind the object. Your shadow grows longer as the Sun sets lower. A cardboard box blocks light completely, casting dark shadows. A glass window lets light pass through, casting no shadow. Let's make funny hand shadows on the wall tonight! For instance, consider the example of Shadow Fact: A shadow always forms on the opposite side of the light source. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Shadow Fact: A shadow always forms on the opposite side of the light source.

Slide 7: Force and Movement
  Text: Objects around us stay still unless we move them. We move objects by applying a push or a pull. A push moves an object away from your body. A pull moves an object closer to your body. Pushing a toy cart makes it roll forward across floors. Pulling a rope brings a bucket of water up wells. Force changes how fast or where an object goes. Identify three pushes or pulls you do every morning! For instance, consider the example of Force: Kicking a soccer ball is a push that changes its speed. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Force: Kicking a soccer ball is a push that changes its speed.

Slide 8: Heat and Energy
  Text: Heat is a form of energy that makes things warm. It changes the state of materials during heating. Butter changes from a solid to a liquid in warm pans. This change of state from solid to liquid is melting. Water bubbles and turns to steam when boiled on stoves. This change of state from liquid to gas is boiling. Heat is essential for cooking our daily food safely. Observe how a raw egg cooks and changes color in pans! For instance, consider the example of Melting: Solid ice melts into liquid water when exposed to solar heat. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Melting: Solid ice melts into liquid water when exposed to solar heat.

Slide 9: Rainbows in the Sky
  Text: Rainbows are beautiful colors that appear after rain. They form when sunlight shines through water droplets. Water droplets act like tiny glass prisms in the air. They split white sunlight into seven distinct colors. These colors are red, orange, yellow, and green. They also include blue, indigo, and violet shades. This bending of light is called refraction in science. Look at the sky opposite the Sun after rain showers! For instance, consider the example of Refraction: Bending of light waves inside water droplets creates rainbows. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Refraction: Bending of light waves inside water droplets creates rainbows.

Slide 10: Wind and Air
  Text: Air is all around us, but it is invisible to eyes. We can feel air when it moves across our skin. Moving air is called wind in our daily environment. Wind pushes sailboats and lifts kites into the sky. We inhale air to get oxygen for our bodies to work. We exhale air to blow out candles or cool hot soup. Wind can be a gentle breeze or a strong storm wind. Observe how wind moves the leaves of tall trees! For instance, consider the example of Wind Power: Wind turns wind turbines to generate clean electricity. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Wind Power: Wind turns wind turbines to generate clean electricity.

Slide 11: Soil and Earth
  [Current Image: images/science_w1_img2.png]
  Text: Soil is the top layer of the Earth's surface. It is made of tiny rock pieces and organic matter. Plants grow their roots in soil to stand firmly. There are different types of soil like clay and sand. Loam soil is rich and dark, holding water well. Clay soil is sticky when wet and holds water long. Sandy soil has large grains and lets water drain fast. Explore the soil in your garden using a hand lens! For instance, consider the example of Soil Types: Loam is the best soil for growing healthy garden vegetables. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Soil Types: Loam is the best soil for growing healthy garden vegetables.

Slide 12: Day and Night
  Text: Day and night happen because the Earth rotates slowly. The Earth spins like a giant top on its axis. The side of the Earth facing the Sun has day. The side of the Earth facing away has night. It takes 24 hours for Earth to spin once completely. The Sun appears to rise in the east every morning. It appears to set in the west every evening. This regular cycle gives us time for activity and rest! For instance, consider the example of Earth Spin: Earth's rotation causes the sun to appear to move in the sky. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Earth Spin: Earth's rotation causes the sun to appear to move in the sky.

Slide 13: Rusting of Metals
  Text: Iron objects change color when left wet in the air. An iron nail turns orange-brown and becomes rough. This chemical process is called rusting in daily science. Rust is crumbly and makes the iron metal weak. It happens because iron combines with oxygen and water. Painting iron gates keeps moisture away to prevent rust. Always keep your metal toys dry after playing outside. Observe old metal keys to see if they have rusted! For instance, consider the example of Rusting: Rust forms on iron surfaces when exposed to damp air. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Rusting: Rust forms on iron surfaces when exposed to damp air.

Slide 14: Hygiene and Germs
  Text: Germs are tiny living things that make us sick. They are too small to see without microscopes. We wash hands with soap and water to remove germs. Rubbing hands together lifts dirt and bacteria off skin. Soap molecules bind to oil and wash germs away. Washing hands keeps us healthy and prevents spreading sickness. Always wash hands before eating and after using toilets. Sing the alphabet song while rubbing soap on hands! For instance, consider the example of Hygiene: Washing hands with soap lifts pathogens off the skin surface. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Hygiene: Washing hands with soap lifts pathogens off the skin surface.

Slide 15: Food and Digestion
  Text: We eat food to get energy for active play. Our body breaks down food through digestion to grow. Our teeth chew food into small pieces in mouths. Saliva softens the chewed food to swallow easily. Our stomach breaks down food further using liquids. Rice and bread give us carbohydrates for quick energy. Fish and eggs give us proteins to build muscles. Fruits and vegetables keep our body systems working well! For instance, consider the example of Digestion: Chewing food increases surface area for stomach enzymes. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Digestion: Chewing food increases surface area for stomach enzymes.

Slide 16: Sound in the Environment
  Text: Sound is created when an object vibrates quickly. A vibration is a rapid back-and-forth movement. Plucking a tight rubber band makes it vibrate and hum. Sound travels as invisible waves through the air. Our ears collect these waves so we can hear sounds. Sound travels faster through solid wood than air. Heavy doors block sounds from entering quiet classrooms. Observe what happens when you touch a speaking speaker! For instance, consider the example of Vibrations: Vocal cords vibrate in our throat when we speak or sing. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Vibrations: Vocal cords vibrate in our throat when we speak or sing.

Slide 17: Guided Practice: Observations
  Text: Let's practice identifying scientific observations in nature. An observation must be a factual statement using senses. Saying 'The apple has red skin' is an observation. Saying 'The apple is delicious' is an opinion. Scientists only record physical facts in their journals. Use a ruler to measure the height of seedlings. Write down the measurement in millimeters on your paper. Always stick to factual details that others can verify! For instance, consider the example of Factual Observation: The leaf has five points and a rough texture. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Factual Observation: The leaf has five points and a rough texture.

Slide 18: Guided Practice: Fact vs Opinion
  [Current Image: images/science_w1_img3.png]
  Text: Scientists separate facts from opinions during experiments. A fact can be proven true by testing or observing. An opinion is a personal feeling or belief about things. Statement: 'The toy car is blue' (This is a fact). Statement: 'The toy car is pretty' (This is an opinion). Factual descriptions keep science records reliable and clean. Avoid using words like beautiful, ugly, or nice in logs. Let's classify five sentences as fact or opinion today! For instance, consider the example of Fact Check: Factual: 'Water boils at 100 degrees Celsius.' To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Fact Check: Factual: 'Water boils at 100 degrees Celsius.'

Slide 19: Guided Practice: Cooking Science
  Text: Let's observe changes that happen during cooking food. Heat changes the properties of raw materials permanently. Raw egg white is a clear liquid in shells. It turns into a solid white color when heated. This happens because heat cooks the proteins inside. Raw rice grains are hard and dry in bags. Boiling water turns them soft and edible in pots. Spot the science in your kitchen during dinner preparation! For instance, consider the example of Cooking Fact: Heat changes raw cake batter into a spongy solid cake. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Cooking Fact: Heat changes raw cake batter into a spongy solid cake.

Slide 20: Guided Practice: Weather Science
  Text: Let's observe changes in weather like real meteorologists. Keep track of clouds, wind direction, and temperature. Dark grey clouds usually indicate that rain is coming. A wind vane shows which direction the wind blows. A thermometer measures how hot or cold the air is. Write down daily weather observations in your journal. Observe if the wind blows harder in mornings or afternoons. Compare weather details across different days of the week! For instance, consider the example of Weather Tool: Thermometers measure air temperature in degrees Celsius. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Weather Tool: Thermometers measure air temperature in degrees Celsius.

Slide 21: Common Error: Opinion in Logs
  Text: A common mistake is writing opinions in science journals. Writing 'This leaf is beautiful' is not scientific. It is a personal feeling that others might not share. Instead, write: 'This leaf has five lobes and points.' This statement describes physical facts that others can see. Stick to measurements, colors, shapes, and textures. Avoid using opinion words when you record science data. Check your journal entries to ensure they contain facts! For instance, consider the example of Incorrect: Writing: 'The experiment was fun and the liquid looked nice.' To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Incorrect: Writing: 'The experiment was fun and the liquid looked nice.'

Slide 22: Common Error: Explaining with Magic
  Text: Do not explain natural events with magic or stories. Look for natural causes and explanations instead. Incorrect: 'Magic makes the water puddle disappear.' Correct: 'Solar heat evaporates water in the puddle.' Science searches for evidence and natural reasons. Understanding causes helps us make accurate predictions. Always ask what force or energy caused the change. Be a fact finder, not a magic believer, in science! For instance, consider the example of Scientific Cause: Heat energy causes liquid water to turn into gas vapor. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Scientific Cause: Heat energy causes liquid water to turn into gas vapor.

Think about the experiments we discussed in the slides. Can you explain them in your own words to others? Use your scientific vocabulary to describe your ideas clearly. Answer the quiz questions and challenges to test your memory. Keep up the great work and enjoy exploring the world! To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Review Card 1: Practice explaining these science ideas to your family.

Slide 1: Spotting Ending Sounds (CVCC)
  Text: Look at your hand. Let's say it slowly: h-a-n-d. Hear how the letters 'n' and 'd' blend at the end? This is a CVCC word: Consonant-Vowel-Consonant-Consonant. It ends with two consonants that make a blended sound. We call these ending consonant blends in phonics. They are very common in the words we use every day. Let's learn how to spot and spell them correctly. We will search for CVCC words in our environment today! For instance, consider the example of Word Pattern: C = Consonant, V = Vowel, C = Consonant, C = Consonant. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Word Pattern: C = Consonant, V = Vowel, C = Consonant, C = Consonant.

Slide 2: Phonics Hunt: In the Tent
  Text: Imagine we are camping under the dark night sky. We set up a strong green tent on the ground. Look at the word 'tent'. It ends with 'nt'. The letters 'n' and 't' blend together smoothly. Let's practice saying the word 'tent' three times. Feel the blend of 'n' and 't' on your tongue. We spell it as t - e - n - t. It is a perfect example of a CVCC word! To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. Slide 8: Grammar: Pointing to Things
  Text: When we observe nature, we need to point to things. We use special words called demonstrative pronouns. These pronouns tell us if an object is near or far. They also tell us if there is one object or many. The four pronouns are: this, that, these, and those. They help make our descriptions clear and specific. Let's learn how to use them like real scientists. We will practice pointing to objects in our room! For instance, consider the example of Focus Pronouns: This, That, These, Those To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Focus Pronouns: This, That, These, Those

Slide 9: Near Us: This and These
  Text: Look at the pencil you are holding in your hand. You can say: 'This is my pencil.' (one object). Now look at the fingers on your own hand. You can say: 'These are my fingers.' (many objects). We use 'this' for a single object near us. We use 'these' for multiple objects close to us. Both words show that the objects are within reach. Try touching a book and saying: 'This is my book.' For instance, consider the example of Near Examples: This pencil (1 near), These rocks (many near). To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Near Examples: This pencil (1 near), These rocks (many near).

Slide 10: Far From Us: That and Those
  Text: Look out the window at the distant sky. You see a bird and say: 'That is a bird.' (one far). You see clouds and say: 'Those are clouds.' (many far). We use 'that' for a single object far away. We use 'those' for multiple objects far away. These words show that the objects are out of reach. Point to a distant tree and say: 'That is a tree.' Point to stars and say: 'Those are stars.' For instance, consider the example of Far Examples: That star (1 far), Those mountains (many far). To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.
  Example: Far Examples: That star (1 far), Those mountains (many far).

Slide 11: Sentence Engine: Declarative Sentences
  [Current Image: images/english_w1_img2.png]
  Text: A telling sentence is like a small train. It makes a statement to tell a fact or observation. We call this a declarative sentence in grammar. It must always start with a capital letter. It must always end with a period punctuation mark. It has a subject (who or what the sentence is about). It has a predicate (what the subject is or does). Let's build a declarative sentence together! For instance, consider the example of Rule: Always start with a capital letter and end with a period. To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Rule: Always start with a capital letter and end with a period.

Slide 12: Declarative: Spotting the Parts
  Text: Let's look at: 'Matteo rides a calesa.' 'Matteo' is the subject because he is the person. 'rides a calesa' is the predicate (the action). Together, they tell us a complete factual statement. Notice the capital 'M' at the beginning of the sentence. Notice the period at the end of the sentence. Without a subject and predicate, a sentence is incomplete. Always check both parts when you write in your journal! To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems. It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers to build a strong foundation.
  Example: Subject: Matteo
  Example: Predicate: rides a calesa

Slide 22: Guided Practice: Capital and Period

Slide 23: Common Error: Mixing Near and Far
  Text: A common mistake is using 'this' for far objects. If a star is shining in the sky, do not say: 'This is a bright star.' (It is too far to touch!). Instead, say: 'That is a bright star.' If the books are far on the shelf, do not say: 'These are my books.' (They are out of reach!). Instead, say: 'Those are my books.' Always check the distance before you choose the pronoun! For instance, consider the example of Correction: 'Those clouds look soft.' To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives. By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills and learn to solve complex problems.   Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Hello, Grade Three student! Welcome!">Kumusta, mag-aaral sa Grade Three! Maligayang pagdating!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="This week, we will study about nouns.">Ngayong linggo, mag-aaral tayo tungkol sa mga pangngalan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="A noun is a name of a person, thing, or place.">Ang pangngalan ay ngalan ng tao, bagay, o pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We will use examples from our own community.">Gagamit tayo ng mga halimbawa sa ating sariling komunidad.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We will study proper and common nouns of places.">Pag-aaralan natin ang pangngalang pantangi at pambalana sa pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="This will help greatly in describing our surroundings.">Malaki ang maitutulong nito sa paglalarawan ng paligid.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Are you ready to write and read with me today?">Handa ka na bang sumulat at magbasa kasama ko ngayon?</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Let's start the happy journey in our language!">Simulan natin ang masayang paglalakbay sa ating wika!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Goal of the Week: Determine proper nouns and pronouns in community areas.">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Layunin ng Linggo: Matukoy ang pangngalang pantangi at pambalana sa mga pook sa komunidad.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Goal of the Week">Layunin ng Linggo</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Determine proper nouns and pronouns in community areas.">Matukoy ang pangngalang pantangi at pambalana sa mga pook sa komunidad.</span>

Slide 1: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="What is a Noun?">Ano ang Pangngalan?</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="A noun is a word used to name things in the world.">Ang pangngalan ay tawag sa ngalan ng mga bagay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="This includes people, animals, places, and events.">Kasama rito ang tao, hayop, pook, at mga pangyayari.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Around us, there are different types of places.">Sa paligid natin, may mga iba't ibang uri ng pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We have homes, schools, churches, and markets.">Mayroon tayong tahanan, paaralan, simbahan, at palengke.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Each of these places has its own name.">Ang bawat pook na ito ay may kani-kanilang pangalan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There is a general name and there is a specific name.">May pangkalahatang tawag at may tiyak ding tawag.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="These are the two main types of nouns in language.">Ito ang dalawang pangunahing uri ng pangngalan sa wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Let's find out how they differ in writing!">Alamin natin kung paano sila nagkakaiba sa pagsulat!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Example of Area: school, village, park">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Halimbawa ng Pook: paaralan (school), barangay (village), parke (park)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example of Area">Halimbawa ng Pook</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="school, village, park">paaralan (school), barangay (village), parke (park)</span>

Slide 2: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Noun Pambalana">Pangngalang Pambalana</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="A common noun is a general name of a place.">Ang pambalana ay pangkalahatang ngalan ng pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is not specific and refers to general categories.">Ito ay hindi tiyak at tumutukoy sa pangkalahatan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It starts with a lowercase letter when written.">Nagsisimula ito sa maliit na titik kapag isinusulat.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Examples: city, province, hospital, and river.">Halimbawa: lungsod, lalawigan, ospital, at ilog.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="When we say 'river', we do not know which one.">Kapag sinabi nating 'ilog', hindi natin alam kung alin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There are many rivers in the Philippines we can go to.">Maraming ilog sa Pilipinas na maaari nating puntahan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="So the word 'river' is a general common noun.">Kaya ang salitang 'ilog' ay pangkalahatang pambalana.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Can you guess other examples of common nouns?">Maaari mo bang hulaan ang iba pang halimbawa?</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Ominous: hospital, mountain, library">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Pambalana: ospital (hospital), bundok (mountain), aklatan (library)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers.">Mahalagang magsanay nang regular at talakayin ang mga ideyang ito sa iyong mga kasamahan at guro.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Ominous">Pambalana</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="hospital, mountain, library">ospital (hospital), bundok (mountain), aklatan (library)</span>

Slide 3: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Proper Noun">Pangngalang Pantangi</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="A proper noun is a specific name of a place.">Ang pantangi ay tiyak na ngalan ng isang pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It refers to one unique and specific place only.">Ito ay tumutukoy sa isang tanging lugar lamang.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It always starts with a capital letter in writing.">Lagi itong nagsisimula sa malaking titik sa pagsulat.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Examples: Manila, Timog Cotabato, Barangay San Jose, Lake Sebu.">Halimbawa: Maynila, Timog Cotabato, Barangay San Jose, Lawa ng Sebu.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="When we say 'Manila', it is a specific city.">Kapag sinabi nating 'Maynila', tiyak na lungsod ito.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="This is the unique name of our nation's capital.">Ito ang tanging pangalan ng kabisera ng bansa natin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Therefore it is written using a capital letter.">Kaya ito ay isinusulat gamit ang malaking titik.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Remember this rule in every writing activity!">Tandaan ang panuntunang ito sa bawat pagsusulat!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Special: Lake Sebu (Lake Sebu), Mt. Matutum, Koronadal City">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Pantangi: Lawa ng Sebu (Lake Sebu), Mt. Matutum, Lungsod ng Koronadal</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Special">Pantangi</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Lake Sebu (Lake Sebu), Mt. Matutum, Koronadal City">Lawa ng Sebu (Lake Sebu), Mt. Matutum, Lungsod ng Koronadal</span>

Slide 4: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Comparing Writing">Pagkukumpara sa Pagsulat</span>
  [Current Image: images/filipino_w1_img1.png]
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Let's compare the two types of nouns side by side.">Pagkumparahin natin ang dalawang uri ng pangngalan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The common noun is 'country', the proper is 'Philippines'.">Ang pambalana ay 'bansa', ang pantangi ay 'Pilipinas'.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The common noun is 'province', the proper is 'Timog Cotabato'.">Ang pambalana ay 'lalawigan', ang pantangi ay 'Timog Cotabato'.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The common noun is 'school', the proper is 'Koronadal School'.">Ang pambalana ay 'paaralan', ang pantangi ay 'Paaralang Koronadal'.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Did you notice the use of the capital letter?">Napansin mo ba ang paggamit ng malaking titik?</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Proper nouns have their own identity in language.">Ang pantangi ay may sariling pagkakakilanlan sa wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Common nouns remain general in their written form.">Ang pambalana ay nananatiling pangkalahatan ang anyo.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Train your eyes to recognize these two forms!">Sanayin ang mata sa pagkilala sa dalawang ito!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Pambalana vs Pantangi: town vs. Town of Tupi">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Pambalana vs Pantangi: bayan (town) vs. Bayan ng Tupi</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Remember: Special = Capital letter">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Tandaan: Pantangi = Malaking titik (Capital letter)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: Pambalana vs Pantangi: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="town vs. Town of Tupi">bayan (town) vs. Bayan ng Tupi</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Remember">Tandaan</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Special = Capital letter">Pantangi = Malaking titik (Capital letter)</span>

Slide 5: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The Home and Community">Ang Tahanan at Komunidad</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Our home is an important place for all of us.">Ang ating tahanan ay isang mahalagang pook sa atin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The common noun for it is 'home' or 'house'.">Ang pambalana para rito ay 'tahanan' o 'bahay'.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The proper noun is your own specific address today.">Ang pantangi naman ay ang iyong sariling address ngayon.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: '123 Rizal Street' is a proper noun.">Halimbawa: '123 Kalye Rizal' ay isang pangngalang pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Outside the house, we can see the barangay hall.">Sa labas ng bahay, makikita natin ang barangay hall.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The term 'barangay hall' is a common noun in our language.">Ang 'barangay hall' ay pambalana sa ating wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="But 'Barangay San Juan Hall' is a proper noun already.">Ngunit ang 'Barangay San Juan Hall' ay pantangi na.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Look at your surroundings and list down places!">Masdan ang iyong paligid at maglista ng pook!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Community: home (common) -&gt; 45 Kalye Mabini (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Komunidad: tahanan (common) -> 45 Kalye Mabini (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Community">Komunidad</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="home (common) -&gt; 45 Kalye Mabini (proper)">tahanan (common) -> 45 Kalye Mabini (proper)</span>

Slide 6: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The School of Analysis">Ang Paaralan sa Pagsusuri</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The school is a place where we study together.">Ang paaralan ay pook kung saan tayo nag-aaral.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The word 'school' is a general common noun.">Ang 'paaralan' ay pangkalahatang pangngalang pambalana.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We have different rooms inside the school building.">Mayroon tayong iba't ibang silid sa loob nito.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There is the classroom, library, office, and restroom.">May silid-aralan, aklatan, opisina, at palikuran.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="All of these rooms are common nouns in language.">Ang lahat ng silid na ito ay pambalana sa wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="But the specific name of your school is a proper noun.">Ngunit ang pangalan ng iyong eskwelahan ay pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: 'Polomolok Elementary School' is proper.">Halimbawa: 'Paaralang Elementarya ng Polomolok' ay pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Always write it using capital letters!">Lagi itong isulat gamit ang malalaking titik!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of school: library (library - pambalana), San Jose School (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Paaralan: aklatan (library - pambalana), Paaralang San Jose (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers.">Mahalagang magsanay nang regular at talakayin ang mga ideyang ito sa iyong mga kasamahan at guro.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="school">Paaralan</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="library (library - pambalana), San Jose School (proper)">aklatan (library - pambalana), Paaralang San Jose (proper)</span>

Slide 7: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Places of Worship">Mga Lugar ng Pagsamba</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The church is a place for our quiet prayers.">Ang simbahan ay pook para sa ating pananalangin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The word 'church' is a general common noun.">Ang 'simbahan' ay pangkalahatang pambalana na salita.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There are different churches and chapels in the community.">May iba't ibang simbahan at kapilya sa komunidad.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: 'Katedral ng Koronadal' is a proper noun.">Halimbawa: 'Katedral ng Koronadal' ay isang pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is the specific name of a cathedral in Timog Cotabato.">Ito ay tiyak na ngalan ng isang katedral sa Timog Cotabato.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There is also the 'Quiapo Mosque' in the City of Manila.">Mayroon ding 'Moske ng Quiapo' sa Lungsod ng Maynila.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The specific names of mosques are also proper nouns.">Ang mga tiyak na ngalan ng moske ay pantangi rin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Remember to respect all places of worship!">Tandaan na igalang ang lahat ng pook ng pagsamba!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of church: chapel (chapel - pambalana), Quiapo Church (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Simbahan: kapilya (chapel - pambalana), Simbahan ng Quiapo (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="church">Simbahan</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="chapel (chapel - pambalana), Quiapo Church (proper)">kapilya (chapel - pambalana), Simbahan ng Quiapo (proper)</span>

Slide 8: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Health Areas">Mga Pook ng Kalusugan</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The hospital is a place that cares for sick people.">Ang ospital ay pook na nag-aalaga sa may-sakit.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The words 'hospital' and 'health center' are common nouns.">Ang 'ospital' at 'health center' ay mga pambalana.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We use them in general everyday conversations.">Ginagamit natin ang mga ito sa pangkalahatang usapan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="But the specific name of a clinic is a proper noun.">Ngunit ang tiyak na ngalan ng klinika ay pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: 'Ospital ng Timog Cotabato' is a specific name.">Halimbawa: 'Ospital ng Timog Cotabato' ay tiyak na ngalan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It must be written with capital letters O, T, and C.">Dapat itong isulat na malaki ang titik O, T, at C.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The 'clinic of Dr. Santos' is also a proper noun.">Ang 'klinika ni Dr. Santos' ay pantangi rin sa wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Why is it important to know the hospital name?">Bakit mahalagang malaman ang ngalan ng ospital?</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Health: clinic (clinic - pambalana), Manila Hospital (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Kalusugan: klinika (clinic - pambalana), Ospital ng Maynila (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Health">Kalusugan</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="clinic (clinic - pambalana), Manila Hospital (proper)">klinika (clinic - pambalana), Ospital ng Maynila (proper)</span>

Slide 9: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Natural Areas">Mga Likas na Pook</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Nature is full of beautiful natural places.">Ang kalikasan ay puno ng magagandang likas na pook.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Examples: mountain, hill, river, sea, and waterfall.">Halimbawa: bundok, burol, ilog, dagat, at talon.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="These words are common nouns in Filipino.">Ang mga salitang ito ay mga pambalana sa Filipino.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="When we give a specific name, it becomes proper.">Kapag binigyan natin ng tiyak na ngalan, ito ay pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Examples: Mount Matutum, Taal Volcano, Lake Sebu.">Halimbawa: Bundok Matutum, Bulkang Taal, Lawa ng Sebu.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="These are written using capital letters.">Isinusulat ang mga ito gamit ang malaking titik.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Mount Matutum is a famous mountain in Timog Cotabato.">Ang Bundok Matutum ay isang kilalang bundok sa Timog Cotabato.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Examine the natural places in your province!">Suriin ang mga likas na pook sa inyong probinsya!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Natural Area: mountain (mountain - pambalana) -&gt; Banahaw Mountain (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Likas na Pook: bundok (mountain - pambalana) -> Bundok Banahaw (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Natural Area">Likas na Pook</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="mountain (mountain - pambalana) -&gt; Banahaw Mountain (proper)">bundok (mountain - pambalana) -> Bundok Banahaw (proper)</span>

Slide 10: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Historic Sites">Mga Makasaysayang Pook</span>
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There are places that play a big part in history.">May mga pook na may malaking bahagi sa kasaysayan.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The term 'historical place' is a common noun.">Ang 'makasaysayang pook' ay isang pangngalang pambalana.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="But the specific monument is proper in language.">Ngunit ang tiyak na monumento ay pantangi sa wika.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: 'Rizal Park' in Manila is a proper noun.">Halimbawa: 'Rizal Park' sa Maynila ay isang pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The 'T'nalak Weaving Center in Lake Sebu' is also proper.">Ang 'T'nalak Weaving Center sa Lake Sebu' ay pantangi rin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="This is where our national hero was born.">Dito ipinanganak ang ating pambansang bayani.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="We write these historical names with capital letters.">Isinusulat natin ang mga ito na may malaking titik.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Let's visit these places in order to learn!">Bisitahin natin ang mga pook na ito upang matuto!</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of history: monument (monument - pambalana), Fort Santiago (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Kasaysayan: monumento (monument - pambalana), Fort Santiago (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers.">Mahalagang magsanay nang regular at talakayin ang mga ideyang ito sa iyong mga kasamahan at guro.</span>
  Example: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="history">Kasaysayan</span>: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="monument (monument - pambalana), Fort Santiago (proper)">monumento (monument - pambalana), Fort Santiago (proper)</span>

  [Current Image: images/filipino_w1_img2.png]
  Text: <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The market is a place where we buy our food.">Ang palengke ay pook kung saan tayo namimili.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The words 'market' and 'store' are common nouns.">Ang 'palengke' at 'tindahan' ay mga pambalana.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="There are many stores in our own barangay.">Maraming tindahan sa ating sariling barangay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="But the specific name of a mall is proper.">Ngunit ang tiyak na ngalan ng mall ay pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Example: 'KCC Mall ng Gensan' is a proper noun.">Halimbawa: 'KCC Mall ng Gensan' ay isang pantangi.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="The 'Store of Aling Maria' is also proper.">Ang 'Tindahan ni Aling Maria' ay pantangi rin.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="These names are written with capital letters.">Isinusulat ang mga ito nang may malaking titik.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="Where do you usually buy your family food?">Saan kayo madalas mamili ng inyong pagkain?</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="For instance, consider the example of Shopping: store (store - pambalana), Rustan&#x27;s Supermarket (proper)">Halimbawa, tingnan natin ang tungkol sa Pamimili: tindahan (store - pambalana), Rustan's Supermarket (proper)</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="To understand this concept deeply, we must look at how it applies to different situations in our daily lives.">Upang maunawaan ang konseptong ito nang malalim, kailangan nating tingnan kung paano ito nalalapat sa iba't ibang sitwasyon sa ating pang-araw-araw na buhay.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="By studying this topic, students can develop critical thinking skills.">Sa pamamagitan ng pag-aaral ng paksang ito, ang mga mag-aaral ay maaaring bumuo ng mga kasanayan sa kritikal na pag-iisip.</span> <span class="fil-sentence" data-translation="It is important to practice regularly and discuss these ideas with your peers and teachers.">Mahalagang magsanay nang regular at talakayin ang mga ideyang ito sa iyong mga kasamahan at guro.</span>
